  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6d39c062-e442-4ada-8464-98838ad2f557'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer2754215793008288419">Popular <i>Gossip Girl</i> character Jenny Humphrey is leaving Constance Billard to attend Waverly Academy, an elite boarding school in New York horse country where glamorous rich kids don't let the rules get in the way of an excellent time. Jenny's determined to leave her crazy Manhattan past behind and become a sophisticated goddess on campus. But first she'll have to contend w</span>
  <span id="freeText2754215793008288419" style="display:none">Popular <i>Gossip Girl</i> character Jenny Humphrey is leaving Constance Billard to attend Waverly Academy, an elite boarding school in New York horse country where glamorous rich kids don't let the rules get in the way of an excellent time. Jenny's determined to leave her crazy Manhattan past behind and become a sophisticated goddess on campus. But first she'll have to contend with her self-absorbed roommates, Callie Vernon and Brett Messerschmidt. Hot guys, new intrigue, and more delicious gossip all add up to more trouble than ever for Jenny. But if getting caught with boys and going up against the Disciplinary Committee is what it takes, Jenny is ready. She'll do all that and more to be <i>The It Girl</i>.</span>

Jenny is the only character who was in the Gossip Girl <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No, I actually read this series before the Gossip Girl series and actually preferred this one. Jenny is the only character who was in the Gossip Girl series and anything you need to know, it tells you in flashbacks.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

I was instantly hooked and it left me craving for more. </span>

<div id="review_288464906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/288464906" />
    <a title="Xela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7844243-xela"><img alt="Xela" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/288464906?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Xela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Xela" href="/user/show/7844243-xela">Xela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer288464906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1175330533119816591">Okay, so I have to admit it. Every time I went into the library, there was always the long row of Gossip Girl books that took up two shelves, and I'd always scoff at them as I went by. I don't watch any of the shows created by this author, and while everyone else is talking about the latest 90210 I'm spacing out about painting my nails or something else I deem more worthy for attention.<br/><br/>However, when I noticed that this other series, a knockoff of Gossip Girl, sitting right next to the Gossip Gir</span>
  <span id="freeText1175330533119816591" style="display:none">Okay, so I have to admit it. Every time I went into the library, there was always the long row of Gossip Girl books that took up two shelves, and I'd always scoff at them as I went by. I don't watch any of the shows created by this author, and while everyone else is talking about the latest 90210 I'm spacing out about painting my nails or something else I deem more worthy for attention.<br /><br />However, when I noticed that this other series, a knockoff of Gossip Girl, sitting right next to the Gossip Girl books, I can't help but pick up the first one, and decide to get it.<br /><br />This book surprised me, because while I'm not that into fashion and shallowness, I liked this book quite a bit. Some of the characters I thought were named ridiculously (cause face it, who names their kid Easy, or Tinsley?) but despite the minor unrealisticness of a few situations, the book caught my attention. Yeah, the characters were a teensy bit shallow, and brand names were thrown around like Halloween candy, but I've already read other books far worse in that department, so this didn't seem too bad. <br />The It Girl managed to be funny and exciting without coming off too idiotic and girly, as most TA books do. The character types were a bit stereotypical and what you'd find in most books (i.e. the bad boy, the nice guy, the shallow diva, the new, sweet girl, etc.) but it was still fun to read. <br />While I may now be sucked into finishing these books (and possibly back-tracking to Gossip Girl) I can still say that this type of book will never be my ultimate favorite and one that I adore.<br /><br />The first type of book I read that was like this was Poseur, and I honestly did not like the series, so I assumed this series would be close to the same. Thankfully it wasn't, revising my view of these type of mindless books that are still fun to read. Coming back for more of Jenny later! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1175330533119816591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2043038399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2043038399" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2043038399?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariel" href="/user/show/21768565-ariel">Ariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2043038399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12765866268867167855">I've never read the gossip girl series, though I've seen the show, so I had a basic understanding of who Jenny was and what happened to her while she was still living in the city (the books are probably different). She goes to Waverly in hopes of a fresh start. A new place, where she can just try to be the best she is. And she really does try. That's where my problems start with her. At least in the show, Jenny was a mean girl. She had a backbone and would stick up for herself constantly. Now in</span>
  <span id="freeText12765866268867167855" style="display:none">I've never read the gossip girl series, though I've seen the show, so I had a basic understanding of who Jenny was and what happened to her while she was still living in the city (the books are probably different). She goes to Waverly in hopes of a fresh start. A new place, where she can just try to be the best she is. And she really does try. That's where my problems start with her. At least in the show, Jenny was a mean girl. She had a backbone and would stick up for herself constantly. Now in this book, she keeps referring to old Jenny as someone who was shy but also outspoken? It gets confusing at times. She wants to blend in here but also wants to please the popular girls and completely goes along with that cheer prank. It just doesn't add up. She needs to pick her role and stick with it, shy or outspoken? Tinsely was referred to so much with such little detail that I'm looking forward to seeing what will happen when both her and Jenny clash, as that's alluded to in the final text messages. I really wanted Callie to get kicked out. She definitely seems the least trustworthy of the bunch, Brett just keeps to herself but doesn't seem to be intentionally mean. I'm assuing Callie and Brandon will rekindle next, while Jenny and Easy explore their feelings for each other. Overall, it was okay for a quick and thoughtless read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12765866268867167855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_100201230" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100201230" />
    <a title="Nour Al Hakim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3333578-nour-al-hakim"><img alt="Nour Al Hakim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271911723p2/3333578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100201230?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nour Al Hakim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nour Al Hakim" href="/user/show/3333578-nour-al-hakim">Nour Al Hakim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100201230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17690108308426451032">Have you ever encountered a book that makes you want to flip page after page nonstop just to see what happens next? Well, The It Girl written by Cecily Von Ziegesar has written an interesting story filled with juicy gossip, great tone, and an amazing passion between the characters. Writing from her own experience, Von Ziegesar makes this book believable and entertaining at the same time. Published in November 2005, The It Girl is part of a bestseller that young adults will most likely love to re</span>
  <span id="freeText17690108308426451032" style="display:none">Have you ever encountered a book that makes you want to flip page after page nonstop just to see what happens next? Well, The It Girl written by Cecily Von Ziegesar has written an interesting story filled with juicy gossip, great tone, and an amazing passion between the characters. Writing from her own experience, Von Ziegesar makes this book believable and entertaining at the same time. Published in November 2005, The It Girl is part of a bestseller that young adults will most likely love to read.<br /><br />Jenny, the main character, is starting a new reputation at Waverly High and she wants to change herself to impress others. Before she even attended the first day of school, crazy rumors have been going around the school campus about Jenny Humphrey. However, Jenny had no idea of what the rumors were or even that rumors were going on about her. Jenny’s mind is set on her new reputation and how she is going to build it. She entered the school right when Tinsley, the girl who everyone loved and was the most popular girl around school, got kicked out. As you move into the story, it starts to become clear that Jenny Humphrey may be the new Tinsley around school. <br /><br />This books has ups and downs throughout the story, but at the end of every chapter is a cliffhanger that builds suspension for the reader making him/her want to keep flipping through the pages. The gossip, drama, and relationships in this story are put into this 256 page book at a medium pace with great and attention grabbing narration. With a love and hate theme, this book reveals each character’s past, giving the reader a general idea about each character as it moves on. The It Girl, a young adult best seller, is a book that you wouldn’t want to put down until you’ve finished it without even realizing how far you have gotten into the book. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17690108308426451032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755339976" href="/book/show/2551274.The_It_Girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202703775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7628104251483135035">I really liked this book. Granted, in a guilty pleasure sort of way as opposed to it being amazing literature but that's only to be expected and I'm only judging it for what it is- light and girly. <br/><br/>I've read but didn't enjoy <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_' title='Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gossip Girl</a> so I wasn't sure how I would feel about The It Girl but it was way, way better. The characters are all really fun and interesting and actually seemed to have a lot more depth to them than I expected. The narration took a little getting used to- it switches charac</span>
  <span id="freeText7628104251483135035" style="display:none">I really liked this book. Granted, in a guilty pleasure sort of way as opposed to it being amazing literature but that's only to be expected and I'm only judging it for what it is- light and girly. <br /><br />I've read but didn't enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_" title="Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar" rel="nofollow noopener">Gossip Girl</a> so I wasn't sure how I would feel about The It Girl but it was way, way better. The characters are all really fun and interesting and actually seemed to have a lot more depth to them than I expected. The narration took a little getting used to- it switches characters randomly in the middle of a page but I didn't even notice that after the first few chapters. <br /><br />The story is good- full of drama and suspense and it kept me reading until the very end because I simply had to know how it ended up. Will I read the next book? Probably, but I'm not sure if this is something I could read a lot of. Overall though, it was an easy and entertaining read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7628104251483135035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16041230002515776515">It was so exciting to see the most human Gossip Girl character Jenny Humphrey get to branch out on her own, getting away from the catty girls at Constance Billard, and having a chance to sort of start over on her own terms.   <span id="freeText16041230002515776515" style="display:none">It was so exciting to see the most human Gossip Girl character Jenny Humphrey get to branch out on her own, getting away from the catty girls at Constance Billard, and having a chance to sort of start over on her own terms. Of course, boarding school is full of the same kind of rich, catty, beautiful girls with their own agendas -- and it seems that wherever Jenny goes, rumors fly around her. Her new roommates are interesting and mysterious: Brett, the secretive redhead who may be starting something up with the sexy young teacher, and Callie, the spoiled rotten governor's daughter who's used to getting exactly what she wants, even from her boyfriend, the arty, slacker boy, Easy Walsh (who you'll fall in love with, too.) Unfortunately for her, Easy Walsh seems to be taking notice of new girl Jenny -- much to Jenny's amazement.<br /><br />Anyone who thought Jenny seemed like a very minor character in the Gossip Girls will appreciate how fully developed (not physically -- though of course she still has her large chest) she becomes once she's out of the shadow of Serena and Blair. She's still kind of awkward in this book, but she uses it to her advantage, and by the end of the book, she has a chance to prove herself as a strong girl that doesn't sit around wishing she were having fun -- she goes out and makes it happen.<br /><br />Plenty of hot guys, love interests, and plot twists that will keep you turning the pages.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer847831492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1786243213785448485">Not normally a book I would go for but I needed something out of the usual fantasy style novels so I chose this.<br/><br/>It girl follows a newbie to Waverly, her name is Jenny and she gets put in a room with two of the most popular girls in the boarding school. She hasn't had the best start though, her stuff has been dropped off in the boys dorm as the school mistakenly thought she was a Mr not a Miss, and to top it off there's already rumors going round that she was a stripper!! <br/><br/><br/>It girl follows Jenny an</span>
  <span id="freeText1786243213785448485" style="display:none">Not normally a book I would go for but I needed something out of the usual fantasy style novels so I chose this.<br /><br />It girl follows a newbie to Waverly, her name is Jenny and she gets put in a room with two of the most popular girls in the boarding school. She hasn't had the best start though, her stuff has been dropped off in the boys dorm as the school mistakenly thought she was a Mr not a Miss, and to top it off there's already rumors going round that she was a stripper!! <br /><br /><br />It girl follows Jenny and her two roomies Brett and Callie through a short easy read of school drama and bitchiness, and it doesn't stop there.<br /><br /><br />Overall It girl was exactly as expected, the writing was simplistic and whilst I wouldn't say it was great story telling it did keep me somewhat interested, mostly because the characters are all relatable. I did have one little issue though, every page pretty much brings up at least one designer name, It got on my nerves quite a bit but I will let it slide because I liked the chapter titles. I did expect there to be more bitchiness and typical high school banter than what was given but maybe thats all to follow in the next few books to this series.<br /><br /><br />I wouldn't rush to buy the next one but its certainly going to be bought for another light read. Im pretty sure the second one will be a lot more gripping though.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Baley Petersen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Baley Petersen" href="/user/show/6334266-baley-petersen">Baley Petersen</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219315436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8393684151445893384">>>Original Post: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://thereadersbookblog.blogspot.com/2011/10/it-girl-cecily-von-ziegesar.html'>http://thereadersbookblog.blogspot.co...</a><br/><br/>I am pretty far away from high school popularity. I attended high school in a very small town were popularity was incredibly relative. I don't recall any one particular girl whom everyone wanted to be or be with, and if that girl existed, she certainly wasn't me. My high school experience was such a unique one that I'm intrigued by girls who are willing to do and say and wear things outside their comfort zone for the sake of popularity. I </span>
  <span id="freeText8393684151445893384" style="display:none">&gt;&gt;Original Post: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://thereadersbookblog.blogspot.com/2011/10/it-girl-cecily-von-ziegesar.html">http://thereadersbookblog.blogspot.co...</a><br /><br />I am pretty far away from high school popularity. I attended high school in a very small town were popularity was incredibly relative. I don't recall any one particular girl whom everyone wanted to be or be with, and if that girl existed, she certainly wasn't me. My high school experience was such a unique one that I'm intrigued by girls who are willing to do and say and wear things outside their comfort zone for the sake of popularity. I suppose that curiousity is what led me to The It Girl. <br /><br />Jenny --a spin-off character from the Gossip Girl series--has transferred to Waverly Boarding School where she hopes to shed her good-girl image, and earn some popularity with her new risk-taking attitude. Thanks to a series of mishaps and little white lies, Jenny fast becomes the most talked about girl on campus. The best-looking guys are all vying for her attention, and her pretty, popular roommates Brett and Callie are fawning over her. Mission....accomplished?<br /><br />The It Girl is one of those books that I couldn't put down, but I couldn't tell you why. This isn't a page turner, full of adventure and action, nor is it a breathless romance. Truth be told, it's a droll little tale of drivel about unreal characters. So I suppose that's a testament to von Ziegesar's writing that she can keep my attention even when the subject is as trivial as high school popularity. The characters are flat and uninteresting, the plot is thin at best, and my interest in the outcome steadily waned from the very beginning. And yet, I couldn't put it down!<br /><br />Rating: $.5</span>
  <a data-text-id="8393684151445893384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_93256645" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93256645" />
    <a title="holly." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3412490-holly"><img alt="holly." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268154653p2/3412490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93256645?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="holly." class="user" itemprop="url" name="holly." href="/user/show/3412490-holly">holly.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93256645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2442647645663452270">I thoroughly enjoyed this book! I found von Ziegsar was completely in-tune with the teenage social scene, and their dialect, customs and ways, so much so it scared me - I felt like I was reading an anonymous guestbook of a ritzy, shockingly scandalous boarding school.<br/>The plot is full of drama, money, and deception. I love how each character is so different, but complements the characters closest to them. Brett, a fierce and modern girl seems to bring out Jenny's warm spirit, whereas Jenny seems </span>
  <span id="freeText2442647645663452270" style="display:none">I thoroughly enjoyed this book! I found von Ziegsar was completely in-tune with the teenage social scene, and their dialect, customs and ways, so much so it scared me - I felt like I was reading an anonymous guestbook of a ritzy, shockingly scandalous boarding school.<br />The plot is full of drama, money, and deception. I love how each character is so different, but complements the characters closest to them. Brett, a fierce and modern girl seems to bring out Jenny's warm spirit, whereas Jenny seems to ground Brett a bit with her soothing capabilities.<br />The character Tinsley is deliciously evil, she oozes sex appeal and is so vividly translated onto the page, I felt as if I were sitting next to her, cold sneer, stunning violet eyes, impeccable clothing and all.<br />The boys are all very well developed, I love Brandon , and how despite how clean-cut, old-money and frantically OCD he is, I found him charming. Heath is filthy, beautiful and rich, complete with a sailor's mouth and an unquenchable desire for every girl he sets his eyes on at Waverly. Easy is a gentle spirit, usually drugged but with his compassionate moments he speaks to every one of the girls the book features - and they listen lustfully, and with intent.<br />Overall, this is the perfect book for a summery day at the beach, a spring break trip to the pool, or just a moment of boredom on a dull weekend.<br />Take heed, do not read this book on a school night. You will be up for hours wanting more and more of von Ziegesar's enticingly delicious work.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2442647645663452270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82067062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82067062" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2465856-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246163290p2/2465856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82067062?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/2465856-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465856-hannah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82067062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16872885281646155429">I really wish goodreads would allow half stars. Because frankly Cecily Von Ziegesar deserves a "pass mark" for her efforts, however, The It Girl doesn't quite deserve a 3. Von Ziegesar manages to write in a steady style: I've never been let down by any of her books, they've always entertained me enough to want to read the next in the series. However, this is no high-class literature. The books are shallow and trashy, and entertainment only in the sense of the gossip they contain. That being said</span>
  <span id="freeText16872885281646155429" style="display:none">I really wish goodreads would allow half stars. Because frankly Cecily Von Ziegesar deserves a "pass mark" for her efforts, however, The It Girl doesn't quite deserve a 3. Von Ziegesar manages to write in a steady style: I've never been let down by any of her books, they've always entertained me enough to want to read the next in the series. However, this is no high-class literature. The books are shallow and trashy, and entertainment only in the sense of the gossip they contain. That being said, for her ability to continue to get them out edition after edition, and never disappoint as many authors with spanning series tend to do, Von Ziegesar will always deserve at least a pass. <br /><br />I liked the role Jenny had in this new book, a step up from the original Gossip Girl books where she's almost a background character at times. I also like the new characters, although all rich like the kids back in Gossip Girl and NYC, they have a very distinct new culture, and I'm looking forward to seeing this expanded in future books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16872885281646155429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer418827504521488026">Read the It Girl novels when I was in middle school. I got up to the 7th book and stopped reading because it just started feeling like one of those soap operas on daytime television. Yes, I know you all know what I'm talking about - "Days of Our Lives" the ones you can start watching in your teens and they'll still be on when you get married. The series was just overly drawn out, however for a middle school student these books kept my interest for quite some time, long enough to read all of the </span>
  <span id="freeText418827504521488026" style="display:none">Read the It Girl novels when I was in middle school. I got up to the 7th book and stopped reading because it just started feeling like one of those soap operas on daytime television. Yes, I know you all know what I'm talking about - "Days of Our Lives" the ones you can start watching in your teens and they'll still be on when you get married. The series was just overly drawn out, however for a middle school student these books kept my interest for quite some time, long enough to read all of the books and then wait for the 6th and 7th to come out. I would recommend it to more of a drama enthralled early teen or tween audience because most older teens would most definitely get bored with the annoying back and forth of the plot. There's a fine line between interesting teen angst and just annoying, irritating repetition - the It Girl novels are riding that fine line.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer11490390758719753763">So if you love the Gossip Girl tv show, you are going to love this novel. Jenny was always interesting and stood out a lot from her family, which I always thought was very interesting because of how shy she actually was. This novel really brings in a lot of new characters that the reader learns to adore through the entire novel. Callie and Easy are by far my favorite</span>
  <span id="freeText11490390758719753763" style="display:none">So if you love the Gossip Girl tv show, you are going to love this novel. I have only read a couple of the Gossip Girl books but I have seen the entire series, and one of my favorite characters was Jenny. Jenny was always interesting and stood out a lot from her family, which I always thought was very interesting because of how shy she actually was. This novel really brings in a lot of new characters that the reader learns to adore through the entire novel. Callie and Easy are by far my favorite, but I want to learn more about the rest of them especially the boys because there are somethings that aren't explained that I really want to know in this novel. <br /><br />Longer review to come soon!</span>

<div id="review_45872947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45872947" />
    <a title="Dani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1848181-dani"><img alt="Dani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280515246p2/1848181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45872947?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani" href="/user/show/1848181-dani">Dani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1848181-dani?shelf=high-school-guilty-pleasures">high-school-guilty-pleasures</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45872947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18353716068790738525">Cross-posted from my blog post <a href='http://danidlion.blogspot.com/2009/12/review-it-girl.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a><br/><br/>My Review: The It-Girl is a fun, slightly trashy, guilty pleasure kind of read. The drama and scandal contained within, you just eat up like candy, while there is enough of slightly deeper stuff involving the characters' inner feelings to make it not completely trashy, and more of a worthwhile read.<br/>When Hooked: Early-On. In the first chapter when we are introduced to Jenny, you are drawn in because of you know you either know her from The Gossip Girl series, or</span>
  <span id="freeText18353716068790738525" style="display:none">Cross-posted from my blog post <a href="http://danidlion.blogspot.com/2009/12/review-it-girl.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br /><br />My Review: The It-Girl is a fun, slightly trashy, guilty pleasure kind of read. The drama and scandal contained within, you just eat up like candy, while there is enough of slightly deeper stuff involving the characters' inner feelings to make it not completely trashy, and more of a worthwhile read.<br />When Hooked: Early-On. In the first chapter when we are introduced to Jenny, you are drawn in because of you know you either know her from The Gossip Girl series, or if not already familiar with her, you become curious to what the elusive boarding school she is about to attend will have instore for us.<br />Hookability: (8/10) The hook is a pretty good one. Not an "oh-my-god-I-NEED-to-know-what-happens-next" hook, but one where your drawn in early on, and are eager to see what kind of trouble the girls of Dumbarton will get themselves into next.<br />Writing: (8/10) The story is very engaging and flows well , and I am a fan of how the author is able to tell the story through each of the character's personal thoughts and actions. (As time passes the story will flip on who is narrating, and sometimes we get other character's takes on past events.) My only criticism is the writing doesn't really bring anything new to the table.<br />Characters: (8/10) I enjoyed the drama that sparked from each of the characters' different personalities, though I definitely liked some characters more than others. Jenny: She is likeable and probably the most 'real' which makes her the one you "root for" through it all. Callie: Move on with your life! The world is not going to stop if you don't have a boy toy. Brett: Really? I thought you were the smart one. Tsk, tsk, you should have stayed with Jeremiah. Easy: (Funny name) Very likeable, maybe not "loveable" but definitely likeable. He's cool even if he can be a bit of a jerk sometimes. Side note: I don't know why but I loved Brandon in this book.<br />Plot: (8/10) There really isn't a 'plot' to this series. There are lots of conflicts and events, but no central plot per se.<br />Originality: (7/10) A boarding school, a girl who is 'poor'/not a lot of money and goes to a place where there are dominantly rich kids and tries to fit in, the new girl suddenly becomes mega-popular; all these are all major themes of this book. And lets face it, these are all not one bit original. We've, or atleast I have, seen them a million different times. But in context with the other novels with these themes, the way it is told through the multiple persons is slightly unique.<br />Romance: (7.5/10) The sparks between Jenny and Easy are cute. They won't melt your heart, but they'll put a smile on your face.<br />Ending: (9/10) Cliff-hanger! Color me intrigued. Very unexpected surprise at end that will make you want to go and get the next book right away!<br />Remembrable: (6.5/10) You might remember the basics, or a bit more, but nothing that will "wow" you, making you remember every detail.<br />Recommendabilty: (7/10) This is hard. To a certain, select group of people who like slightly trashy books and don't mind certain possibly "inappropiate" content, then I recommend it to you. Those who read Gossip Girl series, and watch the show will probably love it! I have a feeling though that most people would either get offended, not be "allowed" to read this, or think that there are more "worthwhile" books to be read. Personally I think it's more like a fun, guilty pleasure, but to those about to pick up, uhm, you've been warned.<br />Any particular graphic/violent/"inappropiate" content? Drinking? YES! Lots of underage drinking references? Drugs? Yes. One occurance where someone is smoking, it was brief and was not dwelled on, but it was there. Violence? No. Sexual content? YES! This book doesn't stop at kissing, or even making out. It really doesn't even fade-to-black either. Its not graphic per se, but you definately get the idea. And there is A LOT of innuendos. I read this at age 12, the age I'm saying you should atleast be when reading this, but if I were to put myself in a parent's shoes I could see them making their kid be a bit older to read this. (12+)<br />Overall: (8.10/10) Like I said this is a definite guilty pleasure read. I think there is a heck of a lot more quality YA books out there for the main intake of reading, but if in need of a private school guilty pleasure chalk full of drama, The It-Girl is for you!<br />Cover Comments: I like it, it has the right feel for the book. Nothing really special though. Though if you do have the whole series, or even a few of the books in the series, the spines look really cool all lined up together! (8/10)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18353716068790738525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_318039124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318039124" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6679481-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497299457p2/6679481.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318039124?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/6679481-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318039124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10285468058266742597">Truthfully, there isn't much I have to say. I read this book 'cause it's a cheap thrill and I just need some light fiction right now. Even if it's about boarding-school Barbies. <br/><br/>Anyway, <b>
  <i>It Girl</i>
</b> is a spin-off from Cecily von Ziegesar's hugely popular <b>
  <i>Gossip Girl</i>
</b> series (which has spawned a total of fourteen books, two spin-offs, and a TV show).<br/><br/>The series follows Jenny Humphrey, the short, ample-chested, Serena van der Woodsen-wannabe Brooklyn resident in Gossip Girl. After getting kicked </span>
  <span id="freeText10285468058266742597" style="display:none">Truthfully, there isn't much I have to say. I read this book 'cause it's a cheap thrill and I just need some light fiction right now. Even if it's about boarding-school Barbies. <br /><br />Anyway, <b>
  <i>It Girl</i>
</b> is a spin-off from Cecily von Ziegesar's hugely popular <b>
  <i>Gossip Girl</i>
</b> series (which has spawned a total of fourteen books, two spin-offs, and a TV show).<br /><br />The series follows Jenny Humphrey, the short, ample-chested, Serena van der Woodsen-wannabe Brooklyn resident in Gossip Girl. After getting kicked out of school due to some unsavory gossip published about her in <i>Page Six</i>, Jenny decides to start anew in Waverly Academy--boarding school.<br /><br />Now, this is basically just a repeat of Gossip Girl except that Jenny is the new star, there's a whole new ensemble cast, a new playground, and just many more rules left to be broken.<br /><br />The first book deals with Jenny wanting to remodel herself to "New Jenny" amidst the new surroundings and the new players.<br /><br />We are also introduced to other characters such as Callie Vernon, the daughter of the governor of Georgia, and her relationship problems with her boyfriend, Waverly legacy and art-and-horseback-riding-loving Easy Walsh, and Brett Messerschmidt, a red-head New Jersey native with a plastic-surgeon dad and an animal-prints-obsessed mom, who is <i>also</i> having relationship problems while at the same time, salivating over a new (hot!) teacher.<br /><br />Of course, all of this is topped by the mystery surrounding the expulsion of it girl, Tinsley Charmichael the previous year, a mystery that I think won't remain a mystery for much long since <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the book ends with the return of the Tinsley <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. ;)<br /><br />I must say that for me, this is much easier to read than Gossip Girl. I don't know why but it must probably because it doesn't focus so much on characters' feelings. The writer just gives us enough without giving us too much. <br /><br />I know the novels are ghost-written and I must say, who ever the writer is, they are doing a pretty good job. Although the books lack depth, they are cheap thrills. They make you lose yourself for a few moments, just enough to escape for a while.<br /><br />Five stars for effective writing, minus one star for depth. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10285468058266742597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer958743963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3651361400891802922">Jenny Humphrey is what a good girl gone bad looks like. She was sweet, nice, shy, and still hasn't found her place in the world. But once Jenny moved to the lower West side in Brooklyn, New York, she felt the need to fit in all because of the school she goes to--- Constance Billard. The girls are walking and talking perfect girls straight out of a magazine, and Jenny thought it was exciting to go to school with socialites, divas, etc. Once Jenny met Blair, she thought she had the ticket to it cr</span>
  <span id="freeText3651361400891802922" style="display:none">Jenny Humphrey is what a good girl gone bad looks like. She was sweet, nice, shy, and still hasn't found her place in the world. But once Jenny moved to the lower West side in Brooklyn, New York, she felt the need to fit in all because of the school she goes to--- Constance Billard. The girls are walking and talking perfect girls straight out of a magazine, and Jenny thought it was exciting to go to school with socialites, divas, etc. Once Jenny met Blair, she thought she had the ticket to it crowd, but Blair made it hard for her. Desperate to fit in, Jenny did things she normally wouldn't do like stealing, exposing, embarrassing people and a lot more to overthrow the Queen Bee Blair Waldorf and be popular. Once Jenny got her overthrown, Jenny was the new Queen of Constance; Blair wasn't happy. All the lying, scheming, and plotting finally caught up to her, Jenny was not only ordered to leave New York by her father, she was banned to come back by Blair after the final straw, and she had to transfer to Waverly Academy, an elite boarding school in the country side of New York. Jenny is determined to leave her wicked ways, and crazy past behind her. Now, Jenny will have to figure out a way to pave a way for herself, and make herself known without coming off to strong, slutty, and self centered. But with the way her roommates are, the drama, and emailing going around, that'll be tough for Little J. <br />This is my favorite series, it's a spin off from my other favorite series and TV show,"Gossip Girl". I love how the author just makes a spin off about somebody who was having her own issues within herself. It just kept my mind racing and wanting to read more and more. I can picture every little thing that goes on during the book. Everything was raw and real that I read. From the setting to the plot to the characters, I just loved reading every detail. <br />The only dislike I had in the book was they kept talking about one character but kept her hidden til the end of the book. I would recommend this book for anybody that loves teen drama.It will most definitely keep them wanting more and more. </span>

    <a title="Olivia Monahon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43875769-olivia-monahon"><img alt="Olivia Monahon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466356759p2/43875769.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1326306459?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia Monahon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia Monahon" href="/user/show/43875769-olivia-monahon">Olivia Monahon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43875769-olivia-monahon?shelf=finished">finished</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1326306459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17300231473509506227">The It Girl is the first book in the It Girl Series. It is written by the same author who wrote the popular book and tv show series Gossip Girl. The story is told through the eyes of Jenny Humphrey, Callie Vernon, Easy Walsh and Brett Messerschmidt, who are all students at the prestigious Waverly Academy. The book starts through Jenny's eyes, as she leaves her cozy home in Brooklyn and her status as the It Girl at Constance Billard Highschool. She then meets her new roommates Callie and Brett. T</span>
  <span id="freeText17300231473509506227" style="display:none">The It Girl is the first book in the It Girl Series. It is written by the same author who wrote the popular book and tv show series Gossip Girl. The story is told through the eyes of Jenny Humphrey, Callie Vernon, Easy Walsh and Brett Messerschmidt, who are all students at the prestigious Waverly Academy. The book starts through Jenny's eyes, as she leaves her cozy home in Brooklyn and her status as the It Girl at Constance Billard Highschool. She then meets her new roommates Callie and Brett. The year before, Callie and Brett were best friends with a girl named Tinsley Carmichael. One night the three were caught with Ectasy and the dean of the school, Dean Marymount, expelled Tinsley. Naturally, this adds tension between Brett and Callie. They both think the other one turned in Tinsley, though they will never voice their opinions. To add to the tension in Callie's life, over the summer she told her boyfriend Easy Walsh she was in love with him and he did not say it back. Back at school, Callie is still watched with a close eye because of the drug mishap. She quickly lies to her teachers telling them that she and Easy broke up, so that she would not be associated with the trouble making he does. She instructs Easy and Jenny to flirt with each other so that the teachers will believe her story. Meanwhile, through all this, Brett is trying to hide to very serious secrets from her peers. The book leaves at a cliff hanger. I found this book very entertaining and well written. I would recommend this series to anyone who enjoyed the series Gossip Girl or is looking for a good book series to get into!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17300231473509506227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asia A." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asia A." href="/user/show/2742796-asia-a">Asia A.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2742796-asia-a?shelf=the-it-girl">the-it-girl</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72652012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6102033518951884351">The It Girl by Cecily Von Ziegesar is a contemporary novel set in Rhinecliff, NY at the luxurious Waverly Academy Boarding School. Cecily writes about protagonist Jenny Humphrey, a character who is determined to break free of her risqué past and start all over. She comes from Constance Billard Academy, the school where the bestseller Gossip Girl series takes place. I really liked this book because it was contemporary and I could relate to the characters. I also like how the author vividly descri</span>
  <span id="freeText6102033518951884351" style="display:none">The It Girl by Cecily Von Ziegesar is a contemporary novel set in Rhinecliff, NY at the luxurious Waverly Academy Boarding School. Cecily writes about protagonist Jenny Humphrey, a character who is determined to break free of her risqué past and start all over. She comes from Constance Billard Academy, the school where the bestseller Gossip Girl series takes place. I really liked this book because it was contemporary and I could relate to the characters. I also like how the author vividly describes what each character is wearing; for example, Von Ziegesar writes, “…She slipped on her own Banana-Republic-but-looks-like-Theory shiny khaki circle skirt, and a pair of baby-pink Cynthia Rowley ballet flats.” (Von Ziegesar, 103). However, I think this book could have been better if it was a little more realistic. In other words there was WAY too much drama. Every other page, there was another fight between protagonist Jenny and antagonist Callie, or Callie and another character named Brett. I would definitely recommend this book to any fans of Gossip Girl, though, considering it’s very similar. Although the book has its faults, I am really looking forward to the other books in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6102033518951884351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476913213?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleigh" href="/user/show/15454202-ashleigh">Ashleigh</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/22002725-the-it-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15454202-ashleigh?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476913213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16660033805704279428">Second read: May 2019<br/><br/>After being kicked out of Constance Billard in New York, Jenny Humphrey is arriving for her first year at Waverley, an elite boarding school, full of beautiful kids. Beautiful rich kids who don't care about the rules, and spend all their times gossiping and hooking up with each other. Jenny finds herself rooming with two of the most girls in school, Callie and Brett, and is instantly thrust into life with the popular kids. <br/><br/>So when I first read this book, I was a lot younger </span>
  <span id="freeText16660033805704279428" style="display:none">Second read: May 2019<br /><br />After being kicked out of Constance Billard in New York, Jenny Humphrey is arriving for her first year at Waverley, an elite boarding school, full of beautiful kids. Beautiful rich kids who don't care about the rules, and spend all their times gossiping and hooking up with each other. Jenny finds herself rooming with two of the most girls in school, Callie and Brett, and is instantly thrust into life with the popular kids. <br /><br />So when I first read this book, I was a lot younger and I loved the series. Who doesn't love reading about rich beautiful self-centred kids partying and making bad decisions? I ate that shit up when I was younger. But re-reading it has made me changed my opinion slightly. I forgot just how self-centred and materialistic this people are. What's worse is that even though I hated 95% of the cast, I couldn't put it down! Urgh, damn you brain! <br /><br />Might continue re-reading this series if I need a filler read..</span>
  <a data-text-id="16660033805704279428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HATJ5PtLkuxvPR1xk0jZWw875Dpsx5GBJxdvLKbymNB/lo9JdePc6tFTs9o+MmtVYSKQU/sPjcusyXZAjjlLww==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7v7zQWNx1gspjeq7P0K8tRAgxghnjUeC5WLUO6/JgeuNbLXs7dmYDZfjRBCSOA67fjmyYfBFW8huvM1XhwJS+A==')})
  }
//]]>
